[۳۰۲. ۱۸. ] فصل : [ في المضاف ] C أما المضاف فهو الذي ماهية معقولة بالقياس إلى غيره ؛ وقد يقال إنه هو الذي ماهية معقولة بالقياس إلى الغير. والأول أولى لما أنه بحسب المعنى دون اللفظ على خلاف الثاني. والأمور المشتركة في هذين التعريفين على ضربين أحدهما ما له ماهية ليست مضافة من حيث ذاتها ولكن يلحقها الإضافة كالرأس مثلا فإن له ماهية هو بها جسم مخصوص، وذلك لا يكون مضافًا حقيقيا من هذا الوجه؛ ثم يلحقه إضافة / إلى البدن الذي هو رأسه؛ وهذا الضرب لا يكون مضافًا. وثانيهما هو الذي ليس له ماهية سوى أنه مضاف أي معقولة الماهية بالقياس إلى غيره الأبوة مثلا لا كالأب فليس لها ماهية سوى القياس والإضافة إلى البنوة؛ وهذا هو المضاف الحقيقي وهو الذي لا وجود له سوی ما به مضاف. والضرب الأول من المضاف ; فذلك بالنظر إلى ما يعرض له من الإضافة إلى غيره لا بالنظر إلى ماهيته فذلك هو الحقيقي أيضًا. والحقيقي في الحقيقة هو الذي لا قوام له بذاته بل هو عارض لغيره من الماهيات. فإذا قطع النظر عن الماهية نفي من الجملة ما هو نفس المضاف الحقيقي. والجملة أعني الماهية مع ما يعرض لها من الإضافة هي من القسم الأول الذي ليس بمضاف حقيقي. ثم الوقوف على المضافات أوقع في الذهن من الوقوف على مجرد الإضافات التي هي المقولة، والأمور التي هي من المضافات فهي الأمور التي ماهياتها مقولة بالقياس إلى غيرها على الإطلاق أو بنحو آخر من أنحاء النسبة. والتي على الإطلاق فهي الأمور التي أسماؤها تدل على كمال معناها من حيث هي مضافة نحو الأخ. وأما التي بنحو آخر فهي التي تعلق بها النسبة فيصير لذلك مضافة مثل القوة من حيث هي لذي قوة والعلم من حيث هو للعالم: فإنهما وما هو بمثلهما في الذات من الكيفيات وإن كانت مضافة؛ فالعلم والقدرة وما أشبه ذلك. وإن كان كله مضافًا فكله في نفسه غير مضاف
[302.18.] Chapter: On the Relative. C. As for the relative, it is that whose quiddity is conceived by relation to another; and it is said that it is that whose quiddity is conceived by relation to the other. The first is more appropriate because it is according to meaning not wording, contrary to the second. The things common to these two definitions are of two types: one is that which has a quiddity that is not relative in itself but relation attaches to it, like the head for example, for it has a quiddity by which it is a specific body, and that is not a true relative in this respect; then relation attaches to the body which is its head; this type is not relative. The second is that which has no quiddity other than being relative, i.e., its quiddity conceived by relation to another, like fatherhood, not like the father, for it has no quiddity other than relation and attachment to sonship; this is the true relative, and it has no existence except what it is relative to. The first type of relative: that is by consideration of what occurs to it of relation to another, not by consideration of its quiddity; so that is also the true [relative]. The true [relative] in reality is that which has no subsistence in itself but is accidental to other quiddities. Therefore if one disregards the quiddity, what is the very true relative is denied from the aggregate. The aggregate, I mean the quiddity with what occurs to it of relation, belongs to the first category which is not a true relative. Then the comprehension of relatives is more impactful in the mind than the comprehension of mere relations which are the category. And the things that are from the relatives are the things whose quiddities are said in relation to another absolutely or in another way of relation. Those absolutely are the things whose names indicate the completeness of their meaning insofar as they are relative, like brother. As for those in another way, they are those to which the relation attaches so they become relative, like power insofar as it is to the powerful, and knowledge insofar as it is to the knower: for these and what resembles them in essence are from the qualities even though they are relative; knowledge, power, and the like. Although all are relative, in themselves they are not relative.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory treatment of the category of relation (al-mudaf). The author begins with a definition: the relative is that whose quiddity is conceived by relation to another. He notes two definitions, preferring the first because it focuses on meaning rather than wording. The things falling under these definitions are divided into two types. The first type has a quiddity that is not relative in itself, but relation attaches to it, like the head: the head has a quiddity of being a specific body, and relation to the body is accidental. This type is not a true relative. The second type has no quiddity other than being relative, like fatherhood: fatherhood has no meaning except relation to sonship. This is the true relative, existing only insofar as it is relative. The author clarifies that the first type can also be considered true relative when viewed from the aspect of the attached relation. However, the true relative in reality is that which has no subsistence in itself. The passage then notes that comprehending relatives is more effective than comprehending mere relations as a category. Finally, it distinguishes two subtypes of relatives: those named absolutely indicating complete meaning as relative (like 'brother'), and those where relation attaches to a quality (like power, knowledge), making them relative although in themselves they are qualities.

Key Terms

المضاف الحقيقي
الإضافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, which of the following is an example of a true relative (al-mudaf al-haqiqi)?
A) Head in relation to body
B) Knowledge in relation to knower
C) Fatherhood in relation to sonship
D) Power in relation to powerful

Key Takeaway
The true relative has no quiddity other than its relation; accidental relatives have an independent quiddity that acquires relation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Categorize each of the following as true relative (essential) or accidental relative: (a) brotherhood in relation to a brother, (b) headship in relation to a body, (c) knowledge in relation to a knower. Justify using the author's criterion of quiddity.
?
In a fiqh text, 'sale' is defined as 'the exchange of property for property by mutual consent'. Identify which aspects are essential relations (linking seller, buyer, property) and which are accidental.
